+Jamison Brereton

2 (622)
Indra (1тАУ40), VibhinduтАЩs Da╠Дnastuti (41тАУ42)
Medh─Бtithi K─Бс╣Зva and Priyamedha ─Ас╣Еgirasa (1тАУ40), Medh─Бtithi K─Бс╣Зva (41тАУ42) 42 verses: g─Бyatr─л, except anuс╣гс╣нubh 28, arranged in trcas. ╠е
As noted above, this hymn has considerably more verses than the preceding one, and is therefore apparently out of sequence. The discrepancy in length between the two hymns is one reason Oldenberg suggests that VIII.1 may have lost verses in transmission. (See the introduction to the preceding hymn.)
As indicated by the Anukramaс╣З─л, the majority of the hymn is devoted to Indra, with the final verses a d─Бnastuti; however, despite the Anukramaс╣З─лтАЩs division, the d─Бnastuti must begin with verse 40, not 41, both because of the tr╠еca division and on grounds of content and tone. In the Indra portion the focus remains almost exclusively on the preparation of soma in its various forms, and the hope that Indra will come to our sacrifice, drink of our soma, and reward us. As often in such hymns, there is a journey component (esp. vss. 19, 26тАУ28), and underlying the calls to Indra to journey to our sacrifice is the worry that Indra will stay away from our sacrifice because of anger or the appeals of other sacrificers (vss. 5тАУ6, 19тАУ20). There are also some slight indications that the hymn is concerned with a ritual innovation being introduced in some of the R╠еgvedic clans, the Third Pressing, which takes place in the evening and involves soma mixed with milk. There are two occurrences of the word ─Б╠Б┼Ыir тАЬmilk-mixtureтАЭ (vss. 10, 11; see also 9b [─Б╠Б┼Ыir is also found twice in VIII.31, which also seems to contain refer ences to Third Pressing]), and verse 18 seems to imply that the gods themselves are not satisfied with a soma sacrifice that ends with the Midday Pressing. The emphasis on the number three (esp. vss. 7тАУ9, 21) may also support this interpretation, as may the hope expressed that Indra will not spend his evening away from us (vs. 20).
Aside from the thematic unity of some of the tr╠еcas (e.g., vss. 7тАУ9 on the three types of soma), this long first section of the hymn has little apparent structure, and it is also notable for its lack of mythological reference (beyond a few token men tions of Vr╠еtra, vss. 26, 31, 36). But throughout this section there are unusual simi les (e.g., vss. 6, 12, 17, 19, 20) and turns of phrase, including some untranslatable grammatical and lexical puns (as in vs. 3). The loose texture and the lightness and transparency of the meter also help to make it an appealing piece.
The d─Бnastuti (vss. 40тАУ42) is, as often, hard to interpret. In verse 40 the actor seems still to be Indra, who in the guise of a ram had some sort of interaction with Medhy─Бtithi: the language here is unclear, and although there are various treatments of Medh─Бtithi (sic) and Indra as ram in the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa literature, these seem desper
ate attempts to make sense of the fleeting and mysterious reference here. Though it

appears to be Indra who is addressed in a subordinate clause in the 2nd person in verse 40, the 2nd person reference has shifted in verse 41 to Vibindhu, apparently the human patron. Perhaps IndraтАЩs generosity is being superimposed on this human patron. The final verse, 42, like the final verse of the d─Бnastuti in VIII.1 (vs. 34), con
cludes the hymn with a sexual innuendo: two тАЬdaughters of joyтАЭ (a phrase that goes neatly into French as filles de joie тАЬprostitutesтАЭ) have also been given to the poet. These may indeed be two women, but since they are called тАЬmilk-strong,тАЭ it is quite possible that the poet is referring to the two breasts of one woman. If so, this verse responds directly to VIII.1.34, where the woman of the poet praises his member, and recalls IV.32.22-24, with a likewise disguised reference to the breasts of a woman given to the poet in payment for his verse.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

English translation:

тАЬGive of dwellings (Indra), drink this effused libation till your belly is full, we offer it, undaunted (Indra), toyou.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

This pressed stalk, o good oneтАФdrink your belly well fullтАФ
have we given to you, o you who bring no threat.

+Griffith

HERE is the Soma juice expressed; O Vasu, drink till thou art full:
Undaunted God, we give it thee.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWashed by the priests, effused by the stones, purified by the woollen filter, like a horse cleansed in astream.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Rinsed by men, pressed by stones, purified by the sheepтАЩs fleece,

+Jamison Brereton Notes

This is an orphan verse, which cannot be construed grammatically with either 1 or 3, though a mere y├бс╕е would allow it to be the rel. clause to 3, as the initial t├бm of 3a suggests.

‘Tis like a courser bathed in stream.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWe have made it sweet for you as the barley-cake mixing it with milk, and therefore, Indra, (I invoke)you to this social rite.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Preparing it with cows [=milk], we have made it sweet for you, like barley (enjoyed) by cows.
Indra, (we have made) you (to be) at this joint revelry.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

I take g├│bhiс╕е twice, with both the frame and the simile. In the frame it is to be construed with t├бm тАж ┼Ыr─лс╣З├бntaс╕е тАЬpreparing it with cowsтАЩ milk,тАЭ but in the simile y├бvaс╣Г n├б тАЬlike barleyтАЭ I take it as a passive variant of the common figure тАЬas cows enjoy a grainfield (y├бvasa-),тАЭ e.g., V.53.8 r├бс╣Зan g─Б╠Бvo n├б y├бvase.

In c Geldner supplies тАЬlade ich,тАЭ but I read akarma from b also in this p─Бda, in a different idiom тАЬmake X to be at/in.тАЭ The usual idiom is ─Б╠БтИЪkс╣Ы тАШbring hereтАЩ; unfortunately there is no trace of ─Б╠Б.

+Griffith

Indra, I call thee to our feast.

+Geldner

+Grassmann

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬ(We praise him) a universal kind-hearted (friend), whom the pure Soma, the mixture (of it) made withdifficulty, or other satisfying (offerings) do not displease.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Whom neither the clear [=unmixed] nor the poorly mixed nor the (juices) that are sharp
keep awayтАФhim of broad extent whose heart is goodтАФ

+Jamison Brereton Notes

tс╣Ыpr├б- only here in the RV, though it appears later and may also be related to tс╣Ыp├бla- (RV 2x), also used of soma (see EWA s.v.); тАШsharpтАЩ is only a guess, though shared with Geldner, a characterization of soma usually expressed by t─лvr├б- (as in 10b).

In c ├бpa тИЪspс╣Ы is found only here in the RV; if it belongs to тИЪspс╣Ы тАШwinтАЩ, it might mean тАШwin awayтАЩ. Geldner tr. тАЬabstossenтАЭ (repel). EWA (s.v. SPAR) suggests that it belongs to a synchronically separate root тАШlosmachen, befreien, in Sicherheit bringenтАЩ, in which case тАШkeep awayтАЩ would work.

The Friend, whom not the brilliant-hued, the badly-mixt or bitter draught,
Repels, the far-extending God;

Den weder der klare, noch der schlechtgemischte noch die scharfen Somas├дfte absto├Яen, den Ger├дumigen mit dem guten Herzen.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWhom others pursue with offerings of milk and curds as hunters chase a deer (with nets and snares),and harass with (inappropriate) praises.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

When those other than us go hunting him with cows, like
(self-)choosing women hunting (husbands),
and creep up on him with their milk-cows.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

A quite opaque verse. The underlying point, in the context of the preceding verse, is that though our own preparations of soma may not be of the best, Indra will still come to our sacrifice (vs. 5), even if other sacrificers aggressively pursue him with (better-tasting) soma mixed with cowsтАЩ milk. The repetition of two words for cow (g├│bhiс╕е opening the verse and dhen├║bhiс╕е closing it) draws attention to the notion and suggests that the other sacrificers have mixed their soma with milk (the most desirable way to serve soma), while our soma was characterized in vs. 5 as unmixed, badly mixed, or тАЬsharpтАЭ (?).

P─Бda b adds its own difficulties to the verseтАЩs interpretation, esp. the rare and disputed word vr─Б╠Б-. In Jamison 2003 [HPS Fs.] I discuss this word and its contexts at length, suggesting that it means тАШ(female) chooserтАЩ (that is, the bride at a svayaс╣Гvara тАЬself-choiceтАЭ wedding) and is a reduced form of *var─Б╠Б-. This passage gave me pause, however, and in that article I toyed with the possibility that it contains a different word vr─Б╠Б- or else that its meaning had become attenuated because it was moribund. I now think that it is the same word vr─Б╠Б- and that it does here compare the other sacrificers to women chasing husbands, perhaps hinting at the unseemly nature of this pursuit. I take mс╣Ыg├бm тАж mс╣Ыg├бyante as a phrasal verb with a cognate accusative, so meaning simply тАЬgo hunting.тАЭ Note that the accent on abhits├бranti requires it to be part of the y├бd clause, leaving the verse without a main clause and making its dependence on vs. 5 clear.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬMay the three libations be effused for the divine Indra in his won dwelling, (for he is) the drinker of theeffused Soma.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Let the three somas be pressed for the god Indra,
for the soma-drinker in (our) own dwelling.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The three soma drinks might refer to the unsatisfactory types in vs. 5 or to the soma at the three pressings, but most likely to the three types mentioned in vs. 9 (the final verse of the tс╣Ыca of which this is the first). We might think of this as a species of тАЬritual repairтАЭ: the poor versions of soma in vs. 5 are adjusted slightly to produce the properly prepared ones in this tс╣Ыca.

The referent of sv├й in c is unclear. (Note in passing that if read as distracted suv├й [with Holland & van Nooten Rig Veda edition], its first syllable matches sut─Б╠Бsaс╕е of b and sutap─Б╠Бvnaс╕е. However, with Oldenberg I prefer to distract the final word to sutap─Б╠Бvanaс╕е; cf. somap─Б╠Бvan-, whose oblique forms require distraction although they are written with -vn-.) If we assume that sv├й refers to the subject, then it must be somaтАЩs dwelling, whatever that is (the ritual ground?). The only other personage mentioned in the verse is Indra, but it is unlikely to be his dwelling тАФ pace Geldner, who construes sutap─Б╠Бvnaс╕е with the loc. phrase (тАЬim eigenen Hause des SomatrinkersтАЭ). I take it as referring to the unexpressed agent of sut─Б╠Бsaс╕е santu тАЬlet them be pressed,тАЭ namely us.

+Griffith

+Geldner

+Grassmann

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThree purifying vessels drop (the Soma), three ladles are well filled (for the libation), the whole isfurnished for the common sacrifice.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The allusion is to the three daily sacrifices. The three vessels are the threetroughs used in the preparation of the Soma libations: droс╣Зakala┼Ыa, p┼лtabhс╣Ыt and ─Бhavan─лya. The threeladles are the three sets of cups, camaс╣г─Бс╕е, used in the three libations

+Jamison Brereton

Three buckets drip and three cups are well filled
at the same presentation.

+Griffith

Three reservoirs exude their drops, filled are three beakers to the brim,
All for one offering to the God.

+Geldner

Drei Eimer laufen ├╝ber, drei Kufen sind vollgef├╝llt bei ein und derselben Darbringung.

+Grassmann

Drei der Kr├╝ge stehen triefend, drei der Schalen ganz gef├╝llet, Sie, vereint auf einer Trage.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬYou (Soma) are pure, distributed in many vessels, mixed at the mid-day sacrifice with milk, and (at thethird sacrifice) with curds, the most exhilarating (Soma) of the hero (Indra).тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

You are clear, outstanding among many; (and you are) mixed with milk in the middle;
and (you, mixed) with curd, (are) the most invigorating for the champion.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

There are successive gappings here: we need to supply asi with b, and asi + ─Б╠Б┼Ы─лrtaс╕е in c. I take all three clauses as 2nd person, though Geldner makes b and c both 3rd person.

+Griffith

Pure art thou, set in many a place, and blended in the midst with milk
And curd, to cheer the Hero best.

+Geldner

Du bist der Reine, auf viele Becher verteilt, in der Mitte ist der mit Milch gemischte, der mit saurer Milch ist f├╝r den Helden der berauschendste.

+Grassmann

Rein bist du, vor vielen herrlich, Soma, ganz mit Milch durchquirlet, Molkenreich zur Lust dem Helden.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬMix, Indra, the milk and Soma, (add) the cake to this libation. I hear that you are possessed of riches.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Prepare these: the milk mixture, the offering cake, and this soma here, o Indra,
for I hear that you are endowed with riches.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

It is a little odd to command Indra to undertake the sacrificial preparations that are really our job. Presumably once again (see VIII.1.19) Indra is conceived of as the indirect agent: by coming to our sacrifice he sets our preparations in motion, and our impetus for this preparation is the knowledge that he has riches to distribute.

+Griffith

O Indra, pour in milk, prepare the cake, and mix the Soma-draught.
I hear them say that thou art rich.

+Geldner

Mische diese, die Milch, den Reiskuchen und diesen Soma, o Indra, denn ich h├╢re, du seiest reich!

+Grassmann

Diesen Milchguss, diesen Kuchen und den Soma, Indra, mische; Denn ein reicher bist du, h├╢r’ ich.

+Elizarenkova

рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рдкреАрддрд╛рд╕рдГ рддреНрд╡рдпрд╛ рдкреАрддрд╛рдГ рд╕реЛрдорд╛рдГ рд╣реГрддреНрд╕реБ рд╣реГрджрдпреЗрд╖реБ рддреНрд╡рджреАрдпреЗрд╖реБ рдпреБрдзреНрдпрдиреНрддреЗ ред рдкрд░рд╕реНрдкрд░рдВ рд╕рдВрдкреНрд░рд╣рд╛рд░рдВ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рддреЗ ред рддрддреНрд░ рджреГрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдиреНрддрдГ ред рд╕реБрд░рд╛рдпрд╛рдВ рдкреАрддрд╛рдпрд╛рдВ рдЬрд╛рдпрдорд╛рдирд╛рдГ рджреБрд░реНрдорджрд╛рд╕реЛ рди ред рджреБрд╖реНрдЯрдорджрд╛ рдпрдерд╛ рдкрд╛рддрд╛рд░рдВ рдорд╛рджрдпрдиреНрддрд┐ рддрджреНрд╡рддреНрддреНрд╡рд╛рдВ рдорд╛рджрдпрд┐рддреБрдВ рдкрд░рд╕реНрдкрд░рдВ рдпреБрдзреНрдпрдиреНрдд рдЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГред рдЕрдкрд┐ рдЪ ред рдЧреНрдирд╛рд╢реНрдЫрдиреНрджрд╛рдВрд╕рд┐ ред рддрд╛рдирд┐ рди рдЬрд╣рддреАрддрд┐ рдирдЧреНрдирд╛рдГ рд╕реНрддреЛрддрд╛рд░рдГ ред рддреЗ рдЪ рдКрдзрд░реНрди рдкрдпрд╕рд╛ рдкреВрд░реНрдгрдВ рдЧрд╡рд╛рджреЗрд░реВрдз рдЗрд╡ рд╕реЛрдордкреВрд░реНрдгрдВ рддреНрд╡рд╛рдВ рдЬрд░рдиреНрддреЗ рд╕реНрддреБрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ ред рдЬрд░рддрд┐рдГ рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рдХрд░реНрдорд╛ рее

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe potations (of Soma) contend in your interior (for your exhilaration) like the inebriation caused bywine; your worshippers praise you (filled full of Soma) like the udder (of a cow with milk).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Like the inebriatioс╣Еdurmad─Бso na sur─Бy─Бm, like bad intoxications, wine, being drunk. This is an allusion to the fermented winesin use, perhaps, according to Manu, an inferior sort of spirit; duс╣гс╣нamad─Б yath─Б pa-t─Бram m─Бdayantitadvatv─Бm m─Бdayitum parasparam yudhyanta ityarthaс╕е; your worshippers praise you: ┼лdhar na nagn─Бjarante: the praisers praise like an udder;

Nagna = naked; stot─Б, a praiser, one who does not neglect orabandon the verses of the Veda, chand─Бс╣Гsi na jahati

+Jamison Brereton

When they have been drunk, they fight each other within the heart, like those badly intoxicated on liquor.
Like the naked in the cold they stay awake.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

A peculiar ending to a celebration of soma, presumably describing some of the potential side-effects of (over-)indulgence in soma.

With Geldner (implicitly) I take ┼л╠Бdhar as belonging not to тАШudderтАЩ, but to a homonymous stem тАШcoldтАЩ, with Avestan cognate (OA, YA aodar-). See EWA s.v. ┼л╠Бdhan-. The same тАШcoldтАЩ sense is found also in V.34.3 and as a pun in X.61.9. But compare Oldenberg, who finds a complex way to rescue тАШudderтАЩ, though not one sufficently plausible to me, anyway. See also disc. ad IX.107.20.

+Griffith

Quaffed juices fight within the breast. The drunken praise not by their wine,
The naked praise not when it rains.

+Geldner

Im Herzen getrunken k├дmpfen die Somatr├дnke wie die in Branntwein bezechten Leute; wie Nackte in der K├дlte bleiben sie wach.

+Grassmann

Die hineingetrunknen k├дmpfen, wie berauscht vom Suratranke, Nahn der Brust wie nackte Kinder.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬ(Indra), the enemy of the unbeliever, apprehends whatever prayer is being repeated, whatever chant isbeing chanted.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Agor arir ─Б ciketa, the enemy of him who does not praise, astutus’ ┼Ыatrur indraс╕е

+Jamison Brereton

Never does the stranger pay attention to a solemn speech being recited if it comes from a man without cattle,
nor to a song being sung.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

As Geldner (n.) points out, this is a subtle jab at Indra. If the god doesnтАЩt provide cows (and other wealth) to his praiser, then no one will pay attention to either the praiser or, by implication, the praise he produces for the god.

+Griffith

Foe of the man who adds no milk, he heeds not any chanted hymn
Or holy psalm that may he sung.

+Geldner

Ein hoher Herr hat noch nie, selbst nicht auf das Loblied geachtet, das ein der Rinder barer S├дnger vortr├дgt, noch auf sein gesungenes Lied.

+Grassmann

Das gesprochne Wort beachtet Indra nicht, des Opferlosen, Noch das Lied, das er ihm singet.

+Elizarenkova

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Note the etymological and phonological figure ┼Ы├нkс╣г─Б ┼Ыac─лvaс╕е ┼Ы├бc─лbhiс╕е. The desire to have a p─Бda consisting of only these related words may account for the absence of naс╕е: ┼Ы├нkс╣гa- regularly takes a dative. Cf. the fuller expression in I.62.12 ┼Ы├нkс╣г─Б ┼Ыac─лvas t├бva naс╕е ┼Ы├бc─лbhiс╕е. Of course naс╕е can be easily supplied here from p─Бda a.

+Jamison Brereton

the Kaс╣Зvas sing to you with their solemn words.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

This verse is a minor but neat example of syntactic modulation. The first p─Бda is in the 1st plural, the third in the 3rd plural, while the middle one is ambiguous: the plurals here can refer to vay├бm тАШweтАЩ in p─Бda a or (coreferential with k├бс╣Зv─Бс╕е in c) serve as subject of the 3rd plural jarante. So p─Бda b, by being without inherent reference to grammatical person, allows “modulation” from 1st to 3rd person. I have taken p─Бda a as a nominal sentence, and b as having third person ref. and belonging with p─Бda c. But in fact the whole verse could be one sentence (as the tv─Б in p─Бda a suggests, since it should be the obj./goal of jarante in Wackernagel’s Law position) with a harsh clash between vay├бm and jarante (which, notice, are the absolute first and last words of the verse, so we can go along as an audience on the happy assumption that the whole verse is in the 1st plural until the rude awakening of jarante).

The bahuvr─лhi tad├нdartha- is a nice example of phrasal univerbation, from t├бd ├нd ├бrtham тАЬjust this (is the) aim.тАЭ

+Griffith

This, even this, O Indra, we implore. as thy devoted friends,
The Kanvas praise thee with their hymns.

+Geldner

Wir, deine ergebenden Freunde, die nur dies eine Ziel haben, o Indra, die Kanviden besingen dich mit Lobgedichten.

+Grassmann

Kanva’s Enkel, deine treuen Freunde, hierauf nur gerichtet, Preisen, Indra, dich mit Spr├╝chen.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬ(Engaged), thunderer, in your recent (worship) I utter no other praise than that of you, the doer of greatdeeds, I repeat only your glorification.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

I express admiration at nothing else, mace-bearer. Like workmen at their labor,
itтАЩs just your praise song to which I pay attention.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

In b I follow a suggestion of RenouтАЩs (EVP 13.98, ad IV.6.4) in interpreting the hapax n├бviс╣гс╣нau as n├б *viс╣гс╣нa├║, with the only emendation the accenting of the second word. Cf. I.92.3 ├бrcanti n─Б╠Бr─лr ap├бso n├б viс╣гс╣н├нbhiс╕е тАЬThey chant like women busy with their labors.тАЭ Oldenberg explains it rather as a haplology of *n├бvaviс╣гс╣нi- тАШnew laborтАЩ (also RenouтАЩs 1st suggestion), and he is followed by Geldner тАЬbei der Neuheit des Dichterwerkes,тАЭ taking ap├бsaс╕е as a gen. sg. But by its accent ap├бsaс╕е should mean тАШworkerтАЩ, not тАШworkтАЩ. K├╝mmel (p. 297) also follows Oldenberg, but, taking account of the accent, tr. тАЬbeim neuen Wirken des K├╝nstlers.тАЭ In the published translation тАЬat their laborтАЭ should be preceded by an asterisk.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe gods love the man who offers libations, they desire not to (let him) sleep, thence they, unslothful,obtain the inebriating Soma.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

The gods seek a presser. They are not eager for sleep.
Tireless, they go to exhilaration.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

pram─Б╠Бda- in c is a hapax, but clearly derived from тИЪmad. I do not understand where Geldner gets тАЬтАж gehen sie auf Reisen.тАЭ Oldenberg, commenting on GeldnerтАЩs same gloss in his Gloss., says тАЬтАж glaube ich nicht.тАЭ

+Griffith

+Grassmann

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬCome to us quickly with excellent viands, be not bashful, like the ardent husband of a new bride.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Drive forth here with prizes. Stop being angry at us,
like a great man with a young wife.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Hoffmann (1967: 87) notes of m─Б╠Бhс╣Ыс╣З─лth─Бс╕е that the prohibitive contains a present injunctive, and he interprets it, plausibly, as тАЬlass ab von deinen GrollтАжтАЭ rather than simply тАЬdonтАЩt be angry.тАЭ However, recent work by Ian Hollenbaugh (presented at AOS March 2017) has argued strenuously, and in my view successfully, against HoffmannтАЩs claim that m─Б╠Бclauses with pres. injunc. are inhibitive, not prohibitive, showing that pres. injunc. verb are found in m─Б╠Бclauses only when the default (root) aor. injunc. is not available. Note that тИЪhс╣Ы тАШbe angryтАЩ only makes pres. forms. The context then must determine whether the form is inhibitive or preventive – in particular, the simile тАЬlike a great man with a young wife,тАЭ the interpretation of which will be severely affected by interference from our contemporary assumptions about such a situation and by our lack of knowledge about the corresponding assumptions in ancient India. If we assume on the basis of popular Western depictions that young wives have many ways of annoying their old husbands (profligate spending, flirting with younger men, etc.), but also have many wiles to win back their husbandsтАЩ favor, then an inhibitive would work.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬLet insuperable, delay (coming to us) today until the evening, like an unlucky son-in-law.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Let not Indradelay: who, being repeatedly summoned, delays his appearance till evening

+Jamison Brereton

Let him not (be) filled with evil rage. Will he spend his evening at a distance from us
like a son-in-law down on his luck?

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The opening m├│ с╣г├║ matches ├│ с╣г├║ of 19a.

On first glance this verse appears to contain a m─Б╠Бprohibitive with a subjunctive karat (so tr. Geldner), which would be grammatically quite anomalous.

Hoffmann (1967: 92) claims that in the Sprachgef├╝hl karat is an injunctive, but this seems extremely unlikely to me because the root aor. of тИЪkr╠еis one of the best attested of such formations, and though the stem k├бra- is well established, there is no evidence that it is not interpreted as a subjunctive. There’s no augmented ├бkara- for example, and no thematic part. *k├бrant- or *k├бram─Бс╣Зa-. I therefore take p─Бda a as an independent clause, with gapped prohibitive copula (тАЬdonтАЩt beтАЭ) with m─Б╠Б. Since the root тИЪas doesn’t form injunctives (or an aorist), there is in fact no way to make a prohibitive copular sentence in any other way.

As noted in the introduction, I think this may be a reference to the instituting of the Third Pressing, which happens in the evening. The point may be that sacrificers who fail to have a Third Pressing risk losing the presence of a disgruntled Indra to those who do.

I do not entirely understand the social relations depicted in c. Ordinarily, in patrilocal marriage the son-in-law would be at a distance anyway; that is, the wife would be living with her husbandтАЩs family. Is this a reference to an in-comer, a husband who lives with his wifeтАЩs family because he’s too poor and who then makes it worse by distancing himself тАФ or to the return of a bride because the husband was too feckless? Or is this similar to the situation in the GamblerтАЩs Lament (X.34), where the husband loses his wife because of his gambling or other economically ruinous activities? In d тАЬdown on his luckтАЭ translates a┼Ыr─лr├б-, which phonologically resembles the characteristic offering of the Third Pressing, the ─Б╠Б┼Ыir- тАШmilk-mixtureтАЩ. It thus indirectly hints at the Third Pressing theme.

+Griffith

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬHandsome-chinned (Indra), the honoured of sages, the doer of great deeds, come, for well-flavoured isSoma; come, for the libations are ready mixed; his (your worshipper) now (invites you) to be present at this socialexhilarating rite.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Na ayam acch─Б sadgana)dan = now this (worshipper) in presence (invites) you to beexhilarated with (us)

+Jamison Brereton

The soma juices are sweet: drive here! The soma juices are
prepared: drive hereтАФ
o you with (lovely) lips, accompanied by the seers, possessed of abilityтАФon your own to the landing site, to the joint revelry.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

n─Б╠Бy├бm is a famous crux. See esp. Thieme (1949) and more recently Jamison 2013 (Fs. Hock), both with discussion of previous literature. After my recent reconsideration of the evidence I would now eliminate тАЬto the landing site,тАЭ since I now think the underlying expression is *n─Б╠Бay├бm тАЬ(just) this man here,тАЭ which lost its transparency and came to mean тАЬon oneтАЩs ownтАЭ and could be used for any person, not just the 3rd.

+Griffith

Sweet are the Soma juices, come! Blent are the Soma juices, come!
Rsi-like, mighty, fair of cheek, come hither quickly to the feast.

+Geldner

S├╝├Я sind die Soma┬┤s, komm her! Gemischt sind die Soma┬┤s, komm her in eigener Person zu dem Gelage, mit ge├╢ffneten Lippen, Rishiumgebener, Machtvoller!

+Grassmann

S├╝ss sind diese Tr├дnke, komme, starker Trinker, S├дnger liebend Zu dem neuen Rauschgelage.

+Elizarenkova

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner takes Indra as the referent of c with magh├│naс╕е acc. pl. referring to human benefactors (тАЬWenn er berauscht ist, so tut er es den freigebigen Herren gleichтАЭ). However, mand├нn- usually describes soma (although it does modify Indra in I.9.2, 101.1, and X.96.6), and the only occurrence of m├бndiс╣гс╣нha- in the RV is found in this hymn and also modifies soma: VIII.2.9 m├бndiс╣гс╣нhaс╕е ┼Ы┼л╠Бrasya “most invigorating for the champion,” with a dependent genitive, which is how I take magh├│naс╕е here. I therefore, somewhat reluctantly take the subject to be soma, who is accompanying (├бnu) Indra, who already contains the multitudes listed in p─Бda a.

However, the appearance of pl. magh├│n─Бm in the next verse (34c), where it refers to humans who receive IndraтАЩs largesse, gives me pause, and it is quite possible that GeldnerтАЩs interpretation is correct.

+Wilson

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬLiberal, wise, (borne by his won) steeds, a hero, the slayer of Vс╣Ыtra, (aided) by the Maruts, truthful, heis the protector of the performer of holy rites.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Wise: or, wise, attaining his object by his steeds

+Jamison Brereton

He is the winner as inspired poet and with his steeds, the smasher of Vr╠еtra, the champion with his superior men,
the real helper of him who does honor.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

In the first p─Бda the grammatically unparallel v├нpro ├бrvadbhiс╕е express the two complementary areas in which Indra is the winner. So also Geldner; see his extensive note.

+Griffith

The Sage who, winning spoil with steeds, slays Vrtra, Hero with the men,
His servant’s faithful succourer.

+Geldner

Er gewinnt als Redner und mit den Streitrossen; der Held erschl├дgt den Vritra mit seinen Mannen, der zuverl├дssige Helfer seines Huldigers.

+Grassmann

Preis erlangt der Herr durch Renner, schl├дgt den Feind, der Held, durch M├дnner, Hilft in Wahrheit dem Verehrer.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬSing, Kaс╣Зvas, the mighty (Indra), of widely-sung renown, the protector of the good, the desirous of(sacrificial) food, present in many plural ces.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

To the lord of the settlement whose fame is from song, whose desire is fame, who has much in himself,
to the prize-winnerтАФsing, Kaс╣Зvas!

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The formation of the hapax purutm─Б╠Бnam is not entirely clear. With Grassmann, AIG III.267 (and implicitly Geldner), it presumably contains the truncated (─Б)tm├бn- stem in one way or another, but I am dubious about the meaning generally assigned to it (Grassmann тАШlebenreichтАЩ, Geldner тАШlanglebigтАЩ), since tm├бn- almost always means тАШselfтАЩ not тАШlife, lifebreathтАЩ, and puru- тАШmuch, manyтАЩ doesnтАЩt seem the most likely way to characterize length of life anyway. I think it possible that it was influenced by expressions like pur├║ tm├бn─Б (I.142.10) тАШabundant in itselfтАЩ, though it is not a straight univerbation. It is also worth noting the long vowel in -tm─Б╠Бnam, given that the only acc. sg. to tm├бnis short-vowel tm├бnam (I.63.8), though I donтАЩt know what to make of this.

+Geldner

Den sangesber├╝hmten rechtm├д├Яigen Herrn, den ruhmliebenden, langlebigen, den sieghaften besinget, ihr Kanva┬┤s!

+Grassmann

Kanva’s, singt dem sangber├╝hmten, preisbegier’gen Herrn der Guten, Lebensreichen Herrn der Labung.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬHe who, a friend (to his worshippers), the doer of great deeds, tracing the catttle by their foot-marks,being without (other means of detection), restored them to those leaders (of rites) who willingly put their trust inhim.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Without other means: or, tracing them, though without their footsteps (to guide them)

+Jamison Brereton

Who as able comrade gave the cows, even though (they were) without tracks, to the superior men
who fixed their desire in him.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

GeldnerтАЩs tr. with added тАЬ(fand)тАЭ (see also his n. and Hoffmann 1967:137) implies that this is a reference to the beginning of the Vala myth, in which the cows are stolen and leave no traces, so that Indra must find them before he gives them away. This interpretation makes sense of the otherwise opaque с╣Ыt├й cid тАж pad├йbhyaс╕е, but it seems to require a lot of added machinery. I do not have an alternative interpretation, however.

+Grassmann

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬYou, thunderer, approaching in the form of a ram, have come to Medhy─Бtithi, one of the race ofKaс╣Зva, thus propitiating you.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

In the form of a ram: с╣вaс╕Нviс╣Г┼Ы─Б Br─Бhmaс╣Зa 1.1: the legend is also found inB─Бс╣гkala Upaniс╣гad; have come to: or, did carry off, ayaс╕е = agamayaс╕е

+Jamison Brereton

O possessor of the stoneтАФhim whose insights are to the point, Medhy─Бtithi K─Бс╣Зva,
since you, having become a ram, led (him) to (goods)тАФ

+Jamison Brereton Notes

This verse as it stands poses a number of problems, but some of them disappear if, following GeldnerтАЩs earlier Komm., adopted also by Oldenberg, and reflected in GeldnerтАЩs tr., the sequence y├бnn ├бyaс╕е (per Pp.) is read y├бn n├бyaс╕е, which requires no change in the Saс╣Гhit─Б text. This produces a subordinating conjunction (y├бd out of sandhi), which in turn accounts for the accented verb (n├бyaс╕е) and allows the whole verse to be read as a single dependent clause (in my interpretation: Geldner supplies the verb тАЬтАж hast du тАж erh├╢rtтАЭ for p─Бdas ab, while Oldenberg suggests rather тАЬdu hast тАж gesegnetтАЭ). Although my interpretation has the y├бd uncomfortably late in its clause, after two heavy constituents (violating HaleтАЩs old observation that only one constituent can precede the y├б-form), it avoids supplying a verb out of nowhere for the first part of the verse, and I take the acc. phrase of ab as an almost extrasentential topicalized NP, so positioned to get the name and attributes of the poet up front.

With Oldenberg and Geldner I take abh├н with n├бyaс╕е, but unlike them donтАЩt supply тАШheavenтАЩ as the goal (on the basis of AV XII.3.16, 17). In the RV the lexeme abh├н тИЪn─л can take as goal v├бsu тАШgoodsтАЩ (VI.53.2) or v├бsyaс╕е тАШbetter stateтАЩ (VI.61.14, I.31.18), and since this verse inaugurates the d─Бnastuti, goods would be at issue.

As noted in the introduction, there are various tales or tale fragments in Vedic prose (see esp. JB III.233-35. also ┼ЪB III.3.4.18) linking Indra as ram and Medh─Бtithi, but to my mind they are later and not particularly successful rationalizations of this obscure verse.

+Griffith

Shaped as a Ram, Stone-hurler I once thou camest hither to the son
Of Kanva, wise Medhyatithi.

+Geldner

Den Kanviden Medhyatithi, dessen Sinn darnach stand, hast du, Herr des Pre├Яsteins, erh├╢rt, als du in einen Widder verwandelt ihn in den Himmel entf├╝hrtest.

+Grassmann

Zu dem wahrhaft frommen Mediatithi, dem Nachkommen des Kanva, komme, o Schleuderer, in Gestalt eines Widders heranschreitend.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬLiberal Vibhindu, you have given to me four times ten thousand, and afterwards eight thousand.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Do your best for him, o Vibhindu, giving him four ten thousands and eight thousands beyond.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the introduction, one unfortunate consequence of taking all of vs. 40 as a single subordinate clause is that the 2nd ps. referent in the subordinate clause of 40 is Indra, while in the main clause here it is Vibhindu, the poetтАЩs patron. As I suggested in the introduction, this may be a ploy to superimpose IndraтАЩs divine generosity on the human patron by implicitly identifying them. Vs. 21 in the next hymn (VIII.3), also in the d─Бnastuti, supports this hypothesis, since there Indra and the Maruts and the human patron Pakasth─Бma Kauray─Бс╣Зa serve as undifferentiated subjects of the verb тАШgaveтАЩ (d├║с╕е).

+Griffith

Vibhindu, thou hast helped this man, giving him thousands four times ten,
And afterward eight thousand more.

+Geldner

Streng dich f├╝r diesen an, Vibhindu, indem du vier Myriaden schenkst und dar├╝ber noch acht Tausend!

+Grassmann

O Vibhindu, gib diesem [Dichter] viermal zehntausend Gaben und noch achttausend dazu zum Geschenke.

+Elizarenkova

рдЙрдд рдЕрдкрд┐ рдЪ рд╕реБ рд╕реБрд╖реНрдареБ рддреНрдпреЗ рддреЗ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддреНрд░ рдкреНрд░рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзреЗ рдкрдпреЛрд╡реГрдзрд╛ рдкрдпрд╕ рдЙрджрдХрд╕реНрдп рд╡рд░реНрдзрдпрд┐рддреНрд░реНрдпреМ рдорд╛рдХреА рдирд┐рд░реНрдорд╛рддреНрд░реНрдпреМ рднреВрддрдЬрд╛рддрд╕реНрдп рд░рдгрд╕реНрдп ред рд╕реНрддреЛрддреГрдирд╛рдореИрддрддреН ред рд╕реНрддреЛрддреБрдГ рдирдкреНрддреНрдпрд╛ рдирдкреНрддреНрдпреМ рди рдкрд╛рддрдпрд┐рддреНрд░реНрдпреМ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рджрд╛рдиреБрдЧреНрд░рд╣рд╢реАрд▓реЗ рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпреМ рдЬрдирд┐рддреНрд╡рдирд╛рдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡реЛрдХреНрддрдзрдирд╕реНрдп рдЬрдирдирд╛рдп рдкреНрд░рд╛рджреБрд░реНрднрд╡рд╛рдп рд▓рд╛рднрд╛рдп рдордорд╣реЗ рд╕реНрддреБрддрд╡рд╛рдирд╕реНрдорд┐ ред рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпреЛрдГ рдкреНрд░рд╕рдиреНрдирдпреЛрд░реЗрд╡реЗрджрдВ рджрд╛рдирдВ рд▓рднреНрдпрддреЗ рдирд╛рдиреНрдпрджреЗрддрд┐ рджрд╛рдирдорд╛рд╣рд╛рддреНрдореНрдпрдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд╛рдзрд┐рдЧрдиреНрддрд╡реНрдпрд╛ рее рее реирек рее

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬI glorify those two (heaven and earth), the augmenters of water, the originators (of beings), thebenefactors of the worshipper, on account of their genitive ration (of the wealth so given to me).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Those two heavenand earth: tye payovс╣Ыdh─Б m─Бk─л raс╣Зasya napty─Б janitvan─Бya m─Бmahe: the substantive is added:dy─Бv─Бpс╣Ыthivau, because, they being plural ased such a gift is obtained, tayoс╕е prassayor evedam d─Бnamlabhyate;

M─Бk─л = nirm─Бtryau, makers, creators;

Napty─Б = anugraha┼Ы─лle, inclided to be favourable; raс╣Зasya,of or to the stot─Б

+Jamison Brereton

And these two dear little ones of mine, the milk-strong daughters of joy, has he bounteously given to become my wives.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Although Geldner declines to tr. m─Бk─л╠Б, the interpretation of this word as a -kasuffixed form of the 1st ps. possessive pronoun, accepted by Oldenberg (see also Scarlatta 519), not only fits the context but would exemplify the tendency to use -ka-suffixed forms in slangy, low-register contexts such as d─Бnastutis. For disc. see Jamison 2009, also 2008.

+Griffith

And these twain pouring streams of milk, creative, daughters of delight,
For wedlock sake I glorify.

+Geldner

Und diese beiden milchreichen ………, die T├╢chter der Lust, hat er zur Ehe geschenkt.

+Grassmann

Und diese beiden milchreichen ausgedehnten [Welten?], die aus der Freude entsprossenen, verherrliche ich um der Nachkommenschaft willen (?)

+Elizarenkova
